### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  02:13:59; model 46.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

All observer variants fail — even `la=1.0, lv=1.0` (full trust in the clean measurement). That's the decisive clue, and it points back to something fundamental: the TVLQR gains are **~70,000**. At that gain, a velocity-estimate error of just 10⁻³ rad/s becomes a 70 m/s² control perturbation. No observer can estimate velocity from sampled angles accurately enough to feed a 70k-gain loop — this is exactly the **sensing-precision-vs-gain tradeoff (κ)** that dominates the whole problem, now in its most extreme form.

So smaller dt opened a *perfect-state* door, but the gains required are too high for any realistic estimator. There's one more lever I haven't tried that directly targets this: **lower the TVLQR gains** (gentler feedback, higher control penalty `r`) — small dt may keep it in the funnel even with looser gains, and looser gains tolerate observer error. Let me test that combination:

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  02:15:22; model 16.8s

Here's the honest consolidated picture of N=6 swing-up after this whole investigation:

## What we learned (a clean three-layer story)

1. **Trajectory layer:** N=6 swing-up nominals exist but pass through a near-straight, near-uncontrollable configuration mid-swing.
2. **Timestep layer (your insight):** at dt=0.01 that made closed-loop diverge even with perfect state; at **dt=0.004 *some* nominals become perfect-state trackable**. So the "wall" was partly a sampling/discretization artifact — I was too pessimistic, you were right to push on dt.
3. **Observer layer (the real wall):** the gains required are ~10k–70k. No realistic observer can estimate velocity from sampled angles well enough to feed gains that large — a 10⁻³ rad/s velocity error becomes a ~70 m/s² control kick. This is exactly the sensing-precision-vs-gain tradeoff (the κ that dominates the whole project) in its most extreme form.

Plus: **fragility** — different IPOPT solutions of the identical problem have wildly different trackability, so even the perfect-state successes aren't robust.

**Bottom line:** a *realistic* (observer-based) N=6 swing-up has not succeeded and sits right at the feasibility boundary of this collocation + TVLQR + observer architecture. This is consistent with the literature topping out at triple/quad. We did get robust N=1–5 swing-up and N=6 balance (delivered).

## Decision point

The honest options, in rough order of effort:

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  02:20:31; tool 15ms

```
26	        return np.concatenate([z[n:2*n], ch.thetadd(z[:n], z[n:2*n], a), [0.0]])
27	    f0 = f(z0); A = np.zeros((nz, nz))
28	    for j in range(nz):
29	        zp = z0.copy(); zp[j] += eps; A[:, j] = (f(zp)-f0)/eps
30	    B = np.zeros((nz, 1))
31	    B[n:2*n, 0] = (ch.thetadd(th, td, a+eps)-ch.thetadd(th, td, a))/eps
32	    B[2*n, 0] = 1.0
33	    return A, B
34	
35	def tvlqr(ch, th, td, a, dt, r=0.1):
36	    n = ch.n; nz = 2*n+1; N = len(th)-1
37	    Q = np.diag([50.]*n+[5.]*n+[1.]); R = np.array([[r]])
38	    P = np.diag([2000.]*n+[200.]*n+[10.])
39	    Ads = []; Bds = []
40	    for k in range(N):
41	        A, B = _linz(ch, th[k], td[k], a[k])
42	        M = np.zeros((nz+1, nz+1)); M[:nz, :nz] = A*dt; M[:nz, nz:] = B*dt; E = expm(M)
43	        Ads.append(E[:nz, :nz]); Bds.append(E[:nz, nz:])
44	    Ks = [None]*N
45	    for k in range(N-1, -1, -1):
46	        Ad, Bd = Ads[k], Bds[k]; S = R+Bd.T@P@Bd
47	        K = np.linalg.solve(S, Bd.T@P@Ad); Ks[k] = K
48	        P = Q+Ad.T@P@Ad-Ad.T@P@Bd@K
49	    return Ks
50	
51	def run(tag, g, dt_sim, T):
52	    log(f"--- CASE {tag}: g={g} dt_sim={dt_sim} T={T} ---")
```

### 👤 **User**  ·  02:58:25; waited 7m33s

What is the core algorithm which allowed the 6 link swingup?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  02:58:47; model 27.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

The 6-link swing-up (perfect-state) came from a **three-part stack**, but one piece was the specific enabler. Let me name each and be precise about which did what.

## The architecture (same as N=2–5)

**1. Direct collocation — finds the open-loop trajectory.**
This is the trajectory optimizer. It discretizes the 15-second motion into ~1500 nodes and treats *every* state and control at every node as a decision variable, then hands the whole thing to a nonlinear program solver (IPOPT) with:
- the dynamics imposed as **constraints** between adjacent nodes (trapezoidal rule),
- boundary conditions (start hanging, end upright, zero velocities),
- bounds (|a| ≤ 25, |v| ≤ 14),
- objective = minimize control effort ∫a².

The trick that made high-N tractable was **implicit dynamics**: instead of computing θ̈ = M⁻¹·rhs symbolically (which explodes combinatorially), it keeps θ̈ as extra decision variables and enforces `M(θ)·θ̈ = rhs` as a constraint — turning a nasty matrix inverse into cheap sparse linear constraints. Plus **homotopy warm-starting**: seed the N=6 solve with the N=5 solution (6th link shadowing the 5th), so IPOPT starts near a good answer.

This produces a *nominal* — a feedforward plan a(t). But you can't replay it open-loop: the system is unstable, so any tiny error grows as e^{λt}.

**2. TVLQR — stabilizes around the trajectory.**
Time-Varying LQR: linearize the dynamics about each point of the nominal, run the Riccati equation *backward in time* to get a schedule of gain matrices K(t), and command `a(t) = a_ff(t) + K(t)·(z_nom(t) − z(t))`. This is the moving "funnel" that pulls deviations back to the plan. (Details in the earlier explanation.)

## The specific enabler for N=6: the integration timestep

Here's the part that's unique to N=6. The collocation + TVLQR stack already worked for N=2–5 at dt=0.01. For N=6 it **diverged at dt=0.01** — and the decisive change was simply **shrinking the simulation timestep to dt=0.004**.

Why that's the core enabler, mechanistically: mid-swing the 6-link chain passes through a near-straight configuration that is near-uncontrollable from a single pivot, which forces the TVLQR gains up to ~70,000. With gains that large, a *discrete* controller updating every 10 ms over-corrects within a single zero-order-hold step — it shoves hard based on a 10-ms-stale error and overshoots, kicking the state out of the funnel. At 4 ms the same gains apply their correction in finer increments, so the closed loop stays inside the funnel through the stiff patch. Nothing else changed — same trajectory class, same TVLQR — just the correction granularity.

So if you want the single sentence: **direct collocation (implicit-dynamics, N-homotopy) generates the swing-up plan, TVLQR tracks it, and the thing that pushed it from N=5 to N=6 was finer-grained sampling (dt 0.01 → 0.004) keeping the very-high-gain TVLQR numerically inside its stability funnel.**

The honest asterisk: this is the *perfect-state* result. The same stack does **not** yet close the loop from realistic angle-only sensing at N=6 — no observer can estimate velocity well enough to feed 70k gains. So the "core algorithm" got us a valid trajectory and a tracking law that works with true state; the missing fourth piece (an estimator that survives those gains) is the open problem.

**🔧 tool → Edit**  ·  67ms
```json
{"replace_all": false, "file_path": "/var/data/inverted-pendulum/repro/optimize_n6.py", "old_string": "#!/usr/bin/env python\n\"\"\"Minimal reproduction (1/2): optimise the 6-link swing-up and emit controls.\n\nPipeline:\n  1. Direct collocation (implicit-dynamics trapezoidal, CasADi/IPOPT) finds the\n     open-loop nominal: hang (theta=pi) -> upright (theta=0), min effort int a^2.\n     Warm-started by homotopy from the 5-link solution (6th link shadows 5th).\n  2. Time-varying LQR (backward Riccati along the nominal) gives a stabilising\n     feedback gain schedule K(t).\n  3. The nominal is resampled to the SIMULATION timestep dt and the closed loop\n     is verified under full-state feedback (it must reach upright); only then are\n     the controls saved.\n\nOutput: repro/n6_controls.npz  (consumed by simulate_n6.py)\n\nCAVEAT: the saved controller assumes FULL-STATE feedback (true theta, thetad).\nThe mid-swing near-straight chain is near-uncontrollable from the single pivot,\nforcing TVLQR gains ~7e4; no realistic angle-only observer can feed gains that\nlarge, so this reproduces the *idealised-sensing* swing-up, not one from real\nsensors. The decisive enabler for N=6 (vs failure at N=5's dt=0.01) is the\nfiner timestep dt=0.004, which keeps the high-gain discrete loop in its funnel.\n\nRun:  uv run python repro/optimize_n6.py\n\"\"\"\nimport sys, pathlib, time\nsys.path.insert(0, str(pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]))\n\nimport numpy as np\nfrom scipy.linal
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:26:57; model 8.3s

The fix worked — the N=2→5 ladder dropped from 170 s+ (stuck) to **13 s total**. The fix was conceptual, not just parameter-tuning: the lower rungs are only homotopy *seeds*, so solving them coarse (25 nodes/s, loose tolerance) instead of fine (100 nodes/s, tol 1e-7) costs nothing downstream — `homotopy_guess` interpolates the seed onto the next rung's grid anyway. Only the final N=6 nominal gets the fine grid.

### 👤 **User**  ·  03:32:11; waited 5m14s

Is this even plausible to do real time, assuming perfect sensors?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:32:36; model 32.0s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Great question — and the answer is **yes, comfortably**, but the reasoning splits into two very different compute phases, and "perfect sensors" hides a second assumption you'd also need.

## Two phases — only one is online

**1. Trajectory optimization + Riccati (offline, one-time).** The ~75 s IPOPT collocation solve and the backward TVLQR recursion are **precomputed once, ahead of time**. They produce a fixed lookup table: the nominal `(θ_nom, θ̇_nom, a_ff)` at each timestep plus the gain schedule `K(t)`. This never runs in the control loop, so its cost is irrelevant to real-time feasibility. You'd bake it into firmware.

**2. The online control loop (must hit 250 Hz).** At each 4 ms tick the controller does exactly:
```
a = a_ff[k] − K[k] · (z − z_nom[k])
```
That's an array index + one **13-element dot product** (K[k] is 1×13). Let me measure it concretely:

**🔧 tool → Bash**  ·  4.0s
```json
{"command": "cd /var/data/inverted-pendulum\nuv run python - <<'EOF'\nimport numpy as np, time\n# online control law cost: a = a_ff - K @ (z - z_nom), K is 1x13, z is 13\nK = np.random.randn(1,13); z = np.random.randn(13); zn = np.random.randn(13); aff=0.3\nNiter=2_000_000\nt0=time.perf_counter()\nfor _ in range(Niter):\n    a = aff - float((K @ (z - zn))[0])\ndt=(time.perf_counter()-t0)/Niter\nprint(f\"per control step: {dt*1e9:.0f} ns  ({dt*1e6:.3f} us)\")\nprint(f\"budget at dt=0.004 (250 Hz): 4,000,000 ns -> headroom ~{4e-3/dt:,.0f}x\")\nprint(f\"max loop rate this allows: {1/dt/1e6:.1f} MHz (vs 0.25 kHz needed)\")\nEOF", "description": "Measure online control-law cost per step"}
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  03:32:47; tool 4.0s

```
per control step: 1908 ns  (1.908 us)
budget at dt=0.004 (250 Hz): 4,000,000 ns -> headroom ~2,096x
max loop rate this allows: 0.5 MHz (vs 0.25 kHz needed)
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:33:04; model 25.4s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

**Computation is a non-issue.** Even in interpreted Python the control step is **1.9 µs** against a **4 ms** budget — ~2000× headroom; in C/embedded it'd be tens of nanoseconds. The loop is a table lookup plus a 13-element dot product. At 250 Hz the real bottleneck would be I/O (reading sensors, commanding the actuator), not arithmetic. So **yes, trivially real-time computationally.**

## But "perfect sensors" isn't quite the whole assumption

Real-time on actual hardware quietly requires three things to be near-perfect, and your question grants only the first:

1. **Sensing** (granted) — perfect state, no observer needed. ✓
2. **Actuation** — here's the catch. The TVLQR gains are **~70,000**. With perfect sensors, a 10⁻³ m/s error in the *commanded* pivot velocity still becomes a ~70 m/s² spurious acceleration. So you'd also need an actuator that reproduces those huge corrections faithfully — high bandwidth, fine resolution, low latency. Finite actuator precision would act exactly like the observer error did and throw it out of the funnel.
3. **Model fidelity** — the feedforward `a_ff(t)` and the linearizations assume the plant matches the model exactly. At 70k gains, even small unmodeled dynamics (friction, flex, mass error) get amplified into large corrections. The controller has essentially **zero robustness margin** through the near-uncontrollable mid-swing patch.

## Bottom line

- **Compute: easily real-time** (microseconds per step, 250 Hz is modest — industrial servo loops run 1–10 kHz).
- **Physically plausible with perfect sensors *and* near-ideal actuation/model: marginally yes** — it's the same razor's-edge that made the observer fail. The 70k gains mean any imperfection in the loop (not just sensing) behaves like sensor noise.
- The honest framing: this isn't compute-limited, it's **robustness-limited**. The reason N=6 swing-up is hard isn't that it's expensive to compute — it's that the near-uncontrollable transit forces gains so high that *every* part of the loop must be near-perfect simultaneously. Perfect sensors remove one of three knife-edges; real-time hardware would still face the other two.

Meanwhile the repro's N=6 solve is still running in the background — I'll report and send the freshly-generated video when it lands.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:54:26; model 18.2s

Here's the honest diagnosis. The mesh-refinement fix **worked for what it targeted** — the ladder is now fast:

- **N=2→5 ladder: 12 s** (was 508 s) ✓
- **N=6 coarse solve: ~6 s** ✓

But it exposed the real problem underneath, the **fragility** we'd found earlier:

- **Attempt 1:** fine-refined fine (~50 s), but the resulting trajectory was **not full-state trackable** → rejected by the self-verify.
- **Attempt 2:** the perturbed warm start sent IPOPT somewhere bad (`inf_pr = 1.7×10⁶` — blowing up).

So N=6 is slow now because it's **searching**: each candidate costs a ~50 s fine solve, and most candidates from the freshly-built ladder *aren't trackable*. The one trackable trajectory I animated earlier came from agent C's *specific* committed N=5 seed; a fresh ladder produces a *different* N=5, and its N=6 children mostly fail the perfect-state trackability test.

**This is the crux:** "self-contained" (your earlier ask) and "fast" are in tension *because trackability of N=6 is fragile* — finding a trackable one from scratch is inherently a multi-minute search, whereas the original was fast only by reusing a known-good seed.

The honest options:

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:16:36; model 19.8s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Still computing the N=6 candidates from the fine N=5. Let me answer your question directly with the actual cost breakdown.

## Why the repro is slow — three compounding reasons

**1. It's solving large nonlinear programs, not running a formula.** Each rung of the swing-up is a *trajectory optimization*: collocation turns it into an NLP with thousands of variables and constraints that IPOPT solves iteratively. Concretely, per solve:

| Rung | Size | Time |
|------|------|------|
| N=2–4 (coarse) | ~100–175 nodes | <2 s each |
| N=5 fine | 1200 nodes, 11-state | ~30–60 s (mesh-refined) |
| N=6 fine | 1500 nodes, 13-state | ~50 s |

There's no shortcut — IPOPT does Newton steps on a big sparse system; that's just what 13-DOF underactuated trajectory optimization costs.

**2. Self-contained means rebuilding the seed.** The *original* N=6 took only ~75 s because it **loaded a precomputed N=5** from disk. When you (rightly) asked it not to take that for granted, the repro now has to **regenerate the whole N=2→6 ladder** — and N=5 is itself a big solve. The work didn't get more expensive; it just stopped being hidden.

**3. The real killer: trackability is fragile, so it's a *search*, not a single solve.** This is what's actually eating the time now. Most N=6 trajectories the optimizer finds are *not* full-state-trackable (the near-uncontrollable mid-swing). So the repro must generate *multiple* N=6 candidates and test each — and I just confirmed the deeper cause: a generic from-scratch N=5 is **lower quality** than the specific committed one, so its N=6 children mostly fail. Each candidate costs a fine solve (~50 s), and you may try many. N solves × 50 s = minutes.

## What I've done to fight each

- **#1** — mesh refinement (coarse→fine warm start): cut the ladder from 508 s to 12 s.
- **#3 cost-per-candidate** — coarse pre-filter + horizon sweep: 8 candidates screened in 99 s instead of ~400 s.
- The remaining slowness is **intrinsic #3**: finding a trackable trajectory is a search, and the from-scratch seed makes the hit-rate low.

The honest tension: *fully self-contained* + *reliably produces a trackable N=6* + *fast* — you can have any two. The original had the last two (reused seed). Pure from-scratch sacrifices speed because it must search. The test finishing now tells me whether a **fine** N=5 raises the hit-rate enough to make from-scratch practical — I'll report the verdict in a moment.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  04:26:37; tool 93ms

```
=== select_n5.py ===
"""Select the best N=5 swing-up trajectory by closed-loop performance.

Tests each candidate (perfect-state TVLQR feasibility first, cheap) then full
closed-loop with the SwingupController across 4 seeds. Picks the one that
succeeds with smallest tail error; saves to swingup_N5.npz.

Usage: uv run python scripts/select_n5.py [n_workers]
"""
import sys, pathlib, json, time, os
sys.path.insert(0, str(pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]))
import numpy as np
import warnings; warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
import multiprocessing as mp

ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
G = 9.81
DT = 0.01
N = 5


def wrap(a):
    return (np.asarray(a) + np.pi) % (2 * np.pi) - np.pi


def perfect_state_ok(fn, preset):
    """Cheap pre-screen: can TVLQR track this traj with perfect state?"""
    from pendulum.dynamics import Chain
    from pendulum.sim import rk4_step
    from pendulum.swingup_traj import compute_tvlqr, TVLQR_PRESETS
    chain = Chain(N, G)
    d = np.load(fn)
    th = d["theta"]; td = d["thetad"]; av = d["a"]; vv = d["v"]; Ns = th.shape[0] - 1
    Ks = compute_tvlqr(chain, d, DT, **TVLQR_PRESETS[preset])
    y = np.concatenate([th[0], td[0]]); v = 0.0; md = 0.0
    for k in range(Ns):
        z = np.concatenate([y[:N], y[N:], [v]]); zn = np.concatenate([th[k], td[k], [vv[k]]])
        a = av[k] - float((Ks[k] @ (z - zn))[0])
        y = rk4_step(chain, y, a, DT); v += a * DT
        md = max(md, np.max(np.abs(y[:N] - th[k + 1])))
        if not np.isfinite(md):
            return False, np.inf
    return md < 0.3, float(np.max(np.abs(wrap(y[:N]))))


def closed_loop(fn, preset, seeds=range(4)):
    from pendulum.dynamics import Chain
    from pendulum.sim import simulate
    from pendulum.swingup_traj import SwingupController
    chain = Chain(N, G)
    T = float(np.load(fn)["t"][-1]); horizon = T + 20.0
    nsteps = int(round(horizon / DT)); tail = int(round(5.0 / DT))
    oks = 0; worst = 0.0
    for seed in seeds:
        rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
        y0 = np.zeros(2 * N); y0[:N] = np.pi + rng.uniform(-1e-3, 1e-3, N)
        c = SwingupController(chain, DT, 0.0, 0.0, str(fn), tvlqr_kw=preset)
        res = simulate(chain, c, y0, DT, nsteps, record=True)
        th = wrap(res["traj"]["y"][:, :N]); te = np.max(np.abs(th[-tail:]))
        if te < 0.3:
            oks += 1
        worst = max(worst, te)
    return oks, float(worst)


def eval_cand(args):
    os.environ.setdefault("OMP_NUM_THREADS", "1")
    fn, presets = args
    out = {"fn": fn, "best": None}
    for preset in presets:
        ok_ps, ps_err = perfect_state_ok(fn, preset)
        if not ok_ps:
            continue
        oks, worst = closed_loop(fn, preset)
        cur = (oks, -worst, preset, ps_err)
        if out["best"] is None or cur[:2] > out["best"][:2]:
            out["best"] = cur
    return out


def main():
    nworkers = int(sys.argv[1]) if len(sys.argv) > 1 else 24
    cdir = ROOT / "results" / "trajectories" / "cand_N5"
    cands = sorted(cdir.glob("cand_*.npz"), key=lambda p: int(p.stem.split("_")[1]))
    if not cands:
        print("no N=5 candidates"); return
    presets = ["vtight", "tight", "default"]
    print(f"N=5: screening {len(cands)} candidates", flush=True)
    args = [(str(p), presets) for p in cands]
    results = []
    with mp.Pool(processes=nworkers) as pool:
        for out in pool.imap_unordered(eval_cand, args, chunksize=1):
            if out["best"] is not None:
                oks, nworst, preset, ps_err = out["best"]
                print(f"  {pathlib.Path(out['fn']).name}: ok={oks}/4 worst={-nworst:.4f} "
                      f"preset={preset} ps_err={ps_err:.4f}", flush=True)
                results.append((oks, nworst, out["fn"], preset))
    if not results:
        print("N=5: NO candidate passed closed-loop"); return
    results.sort(key=lambda r: (r[0], r[1]), reverse=True)
    oks, nworst, fn, preset = results[0]
    print(f"N=5: BEST {pathlib.Path(fn).name} o
… [truncated 2524 chars]
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:27:03; model 32.7s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Now I can answer accurately — and "hand-selected" was my imprecise word; it was actually an **automated generate-and-rank pipeline** (two scripts agent C wrote). Here's the real process:

## Generation — `gen_candidates.py`

It builds a *pool* of N=5 trajectories by sweeping three axes:

1. **Horizon** T ∈ {9, 11, 13, 15} s
2. **Terminal target** — this is the important one. Five different end configurations:
   - `zeros` (all links straight up),
   - `first+2π`, `first−2π` (first link does a full extra revolution),
   - `all+2π`, `alt2π` (alternating ±2π per link).
   
   These are **different homotopy classes** — physically different ways to invert the chain (which links spin which way around). They produce genuinely different trajectory families with very different controllability.
3. **8 random seeds** each.

Each (T, target, seed) is solved coarse (h=0.05) → refined (h=0.01) [mesh refinement], scored by open-loop drift over the first 70% (a trackability proxy) + terminal residual, and every valid one saved to `cand_N5/cand_{idx}.npz`. That gave **21 candidates**.

## Selection — `select_n5.py`

For each candidate × each TVLQR preset {vtight, tight, default}:
1. **Cheap pre-screen:** perfect-state TVLQR trackability (open-loop drift < 0.3 rad) — skip if it fails.
2. **Full closed-loop test** with the *realistic* observer-based `SwingupController`, across **4 seeds** with ±10⁻³ rad initial perturbations.
3. Record: how many of 4 seeds succeed (tail error < 0.3 rad) and the worst tail error.

Then **rank by (seeds-passed, then smallest worst-tail-error)** and keep the winner. For N=5 that was `cand_6.npz`, preset `default`, **4/4 seeds, worst tail 2.5×10⁻⁵ rad** — recorded in `selection_N5.json`.

## Why this explains my from-scratch failure

My ladder generated **one** N=5 (the first that converged) with **only `target=zeros`**. Agent C generated ~21 across **multiple horizons and multiple terminal homotopy classes**, then kept the most *closed-loop-robust* one. The missing ingredient in my ladder is almost certainly the **terminal-target diversity** — the right inversion topology is what makes a trajectory controllable enough to track, and `zeros` alone may simply not contain a trackable N=6 ancestor.

This directly reshapes the nested search you approved: it shouldn't just vary horizon — it must vary the **terminal target** (the ±2π homotopy classes), exactly as `gen_candidates.py` does, and rank by closed-loop robustness. That's very likely the actual key, and it means I should build the nested search around `gen_candidates.py` + `select_n5.py`'s existing logic rather than my thinner horizon-only sweep. Want me to wire the search that way (reuse those two scripts' approach for both N=5 and N=6)?

```
    settle_frac = 0.12

    outdir = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1] / "results" / "trajectories" / f"cand_N{n}"
    outdir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    for old in outdir.glob("*.npz"):
        old.unlink()

    print(f"=== N={n} Ts={Ts} a_max={a_max} ===", flush=True)
    idx = 0
    meta = []
    for T in Ts:
        Kc = int(round(T / 0.05))
        Kf = int(round(T / DT))
        for tname, tgt in target_options(n):
            for seed in seeds:
                t0 = time.time()
                try:
                    sc = solve_swingup(n, T, Kc, g=G, a_max=a_max, v_max=v_max,
                                       theta_target=tgt, seed=seed,
                                       settle_frac=settle_frac, max_iter=2500)
                except Exception as e:
                    continue
                if sc["status"] != "solved":
                    continue
                try:
                    sf = solve_swingup(n, T, Kf, g=G, a_max=a_max, v_max=v_max,
                                       theta_target=tgt, init_guess=sc,
                                       settle_frac=settle_frac, max_iter=2500)
                except Exception:
                    continue
                if sf["status"] != "solved":
                    continue
                track = openloop_track(n, sf, frac=0.7)
                term = np.max(np.abs(sf["theta"][-1] - tgt))
                fn = outdir / f"cand_{idx}.npz"
                np.savez(fn, t=sf["t"], theta=sf["theta"], thetad=sf["thetad"],
                         a=sf["a"], v=sf["v"], T=sf["T"], target=tgt)
                m = dict(idx=idx, T=T, target=tname, seed=seed,
                         cost=round(sf["cost"], 3), track=round(float(track), 5),
                         term=round(float(term), 6), maxv=round(float(np.max(np.abs(sf["v"]))), 3),
                         maxa=round(float(np.max(np.abs(sf["a"]))), 3))
                meta.append(m)
                print(f"  [{idx}] T={T} {tname} seed={seed} cost={m['cost']} "
                      f"track={m['track']} term={m['term']} maxv={m['maxv']} "
                      f"({time.time()-t0:.0f}s)", flush=True)
                idx += 1
    with open(outdir / "meta.json", "w") as fh:
        json.dump(meta, fh, indent=2)
    print(f"N={n}: {idx} candidates saved to {outdir}", flush=True)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:34:00; model 15.7s

Now, to answer your earlier question about **how the seed was selected** (it wasn't literally by hand — it was an automated rank), and to confirm the new script faithfully reuses that approach:

**The script I just wrote and launched replicates agent C's exact pipeline, self-contained in one file:**

1. **Generate N=5 pool** (`gen_candidates.py`'s approach) — sweep horizon × **terminal target** (the ±2π homotopy classes — the diversity my earlier ladder lacked) × seed; each coarse(h=0.05)→refine(h=0.01).
2. **Rank N=5** (`select_n5.py`'s approach) — score each by closed-loop robustness with the *realistic observer controller* across 4 perturbed seeds (seeds-passed, then smallest tail error). Keep top 3 as homotopy seeds.
3. **Generate N=6 pool** — homotopy from each kept N=5, swept over targets × horizons, coarse→refine (the N=6 refinement step).
4. **Select N=6** — the one trackable under full-state TVLQR at dt=0.004, smallest upright error.
5. **Save** `n6_controls.npz`.

The whole thing runs **in parallel** (32 workers — that's how agent C's `select_n5.py` made ~100 solves tractable). It's currently generating the N=5 pool; the monitor will report each stage (`candidates solved` → `KEEP` → `trackable` → `BEST` → `SAVED`). This is the genuine tens-of-minutes nested search you approved, now done the proven way. I'll run `simulate_n6.py` and send the video once it writes the controls.

Ah — I had it wrong. You mean **bend order = the relative bending pattern**: how adjacent links are rotated left/right of each other (the chain's S-shape/zigzag), and when each joint crosses the straight (aligned-with-neighbor) point. That's a much more relevant characterization — it directly relates to the near-uncontrollable *straight-chain* configuration we found. Let me characterize it properly:

**🔧 tool → Bash**  ·  279ms
```json
{"command": "cd /var/data/inverted-pendulum\nuv run python - <<'EOF' 2>&1 | grep -vE \"Warning|self.A\"\nimport sys; sys.path.insert(0,'.')\nimport numpy as np\nd = np.load('results/trajectories/swingup_N5.npz')\nth = d['theta']; t = d['t']  # (T,5)\n# inter-link bend = relative angle between adjacent links theta_i - theta_{i+1}\n# (0 = those two links straight/aligned; sign = bend left/right)\nrel = th[:,:-1] - th[:,1:]   # (T,4) joints between links (0-1,1-2,2-3,3-4)\nprint(\"4 joint bend angles (deg) over time, sampled:\")\nfor frac in [0.0,0.2,0.4,0.5,0.6,0.7,0.8,0.9,1.0]:\n    k=int(frac*(len(t)-1))\n    print(f\"  t={t[k]:5.2f}s  bends={np.degrees(rel[k]).round(0)}\")\n# zero-crossings per joint = when adjacent links align (pass through straight)\nprint(\"\\nstraight-crossings per joint (adjacent links align):\")\nfor j in range(4):\n    s=np.sign(rel[:,j]); cr=np.where(np.diff(s)!=0)[0]\n    print(f\"  joint {j} (link{j}-{j+1}): {len(cr)} crossings at t={[round(t[c],2) for c in cr]}\")\n# overall straightness: max |bend| across joints (small = whole chain near-straight)\nmaxbend = np.degrees(np.max(np.abs(rel),axis=1))\nkmin = np.argmin(maxbend)\nprint(f\"\\nmost-straight moment: t={t[kmin]:.2f}s, max joint bend only {maxbend[kmin]:.1f} deg\")\nprint(f\"min over time of max-joint-bend: {maxbend.min():.1f} deg  (how straight it gets)\")\nEOF", "description": "Characterize inter-link bend order and straight-crossings of N=5 seed"}
```

Both runs are progressing with monitors armed. To close the loop on your bend-order point:

**Your refined definition is the right one** — and it reframes the earlier "near-uncontrollable straight chain" finding. The working N=5 doesn't avoid being near-straight; instead it stays *near-aligned but shimmying* — each joint crosses the straight point 16–20 times in a coordinated left-right pattern during the swing. - The bend order is *emergent* from min-effort + target=zeros, so both live runs reproduce it by reproducing that setup (the main run's 4/4 `N5_zeros_T13` and the bend-match run's T=12 reproduction).

Cleaned up — all working artifacts intact, no stray processes. I need to be straight with you now, because this is the **~8th full attempt** and the pattern is unambiguous.

## Honest status

Both runs failed to produce a from-scratch trackable N=6:
- **Main run:** generated 4/4-robust N=5 seeds from scratch ✓, but 0/2 of their N=6 children were trackable.
- **Bend-match run:** failed even earlier — the N=5 fine solve at T=12 didn't converge.

## What this confirms — your bend-order insight is the crux

The sharpest finding of this whole effort came from your question. The main run proves it: **a from-scratch N=5 can match the committed seed's closed-loop robustness (both 4/4) yet still fail to yield a trackable N=6.** The difference is the *bend order* — the relative left/right bending topology the N=5 carries into the N=6 lift. Matching N=5 *quality* is not enough; the *bend pattern* must match, and reproducing that specific pattern from scratch is itself an unsolved search (the bend-match run couldn't even converge its N=5).

## My honest assessment

A fully self-contained, from-scratch, *reliably trackable* N=6 has eluded ~8 systematic attempts. Each fix (mesh refinement, homotopy seeding, per-N settings, target diversity) removed one barrier and exposed the next; the residual one — reproducing the exact controllable bend order from scratch — is a genuine research problem, consistent with the literature topping out at triple/quad pendulums. More parameter-tweaking is unlikely to crack it in-session.

## What we definitively have

- A **working trackable N=6** (`swingup_N6_perfectstate.mp4`, delivered) and its controls.
- A **reliable repro** *if* it uses the committed N=5 seed — which is itself a legitimate, version-controlled artifact generated by the in-repo pipeline (`gen_candidates.py` + `select_n5.py`), not an external black box.

## Recommendation

Ship the **two-tier repro**: `optimize_n6.py` uses the committed (repo-generated, regeneratable) N=5 seed by default → reliable ~75 s + video; the from-scratch generator I wrote stays as a documented best-effort path with the honest caveat that finding a from-scratch N=5 with the right bend order is a long, uncertain search. That respects "don't take the seed for granted" (the seed *is* regeneratable, pipeline in-repo) while actually working.

Want me to finalize that two-tier repro and commit it — or would you rather I keep grinding the from-scratch bend-order search despite the odds?

Both requests done and committed. Summary:

## 1. Backed up the good N=5 solve ✅
`repro/seeds/swingup_N5_GOOD.npz` (+ its selection metadata and the known-good N=6), confirmed bend order T=12, all links −0.5 rev. Safe from any future regeneration.

## 2. Made it a 2-stage optimization and re-ran ✅
- **`stage1_n5.py`** — from-scratch N=5: homotopy ladder N=2→4, then candidate pool (target × horizon sweep, a_max=60), ranked by closed-loop robustness → seed.
- **`stage2_n6.py`** — N=6 from a seed: homotopy-lift + **direct fine solve** per target/horizon, select the dt=0.004 full-state-trackable one → `n6_controls.npz`.
- **`optimize_n6.py`** — orchestrates Stage 1 → Stage 2 (with a documented fall-back to the good seed).
- **`simulate_n6.py`** — verify + render.

**Re-ran Stage 2 on the backed-up good N=5 → reliably reproduced the trackable N=6**: `VERIFICATION: PASS`, final 0.069°, maxK=69448, in ~1–2 min. Fresh mp4 delivered above.

## The decisive bug + finding
- **Bug fixed:** my Stage-2 coarse→fine was failing 8/9 (the N=6 *coarse* h=0.05 solve is unreliable); the **direct fine solve** from a good seed converges in ~60 s.
- **Your bend-order insight, confirmed and documented:** decoupling the stages exposed that an N=5's closed-loop *score* (even 4/4) is necessary but **not sufficient** — Stage 2 only finds a trackable N=6 when the seed's *bend order* matches a controllable topology. That's why Stage 2 from the *good* seed succeeds while from-scratch 4/4 seeds failed. The 2-stage split makes this cleanly testable and lets you iterate Stage 1 against a fixed, reliable Stage 2.

The reliable path (Stage 2 from the backed-up seed) is now solid and fast. Stage 1's from-scratch seed remains a longer, lower-yield search — its success hinges on reproducing that bend order, which is the documented open problem.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  06:12:12; model 27.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Quantified — and the jerk you're seeing at ~8–9 s is actually the *tail* of a violent catch phase that's worst around 5–8 s. Here's the picture (pivot acceleration, perfect-state closed loop):

| Window | peak \|a\| (m/s²) | peak jerk (m/s³) | peak link acc (rad/s²) |
|--------|------|------|------|
| 0–5 s (swing) | ~5 | ~45 | ~90 |
| 5–6 s | **26** | **4262** | 257 |
| 6–7 s | 16 | 2427 | 360 |
| 7–8 s | **50.7** | 2434 | 50 |
| **8–9 s** | **24** (range −24…+23) | **681** | 27 |
| 9 s+ (settled) | <3 | <33 | ~0 |

So **at 8–9 s the pivot acceleration swings ±24 m/s² (~2.4 g) with jerk up to ~680 m/s³** — but that's milder than the true peak: **7–8 s hits 50.7 m/s² (~5 g)** and **5–6 s spikes to ~4300 m/s³ of jerk**.

Two things worth flagging:

1. **The realized acceleration (50.7) is 2× the nominal bound.** The trajectory optimizer capped the *feedforward* at a_max=25, but the TVLQR *feedback* (gains ~70,000) adds huge corrections during the unstable catch, so the actual commanded pivot acceleration roughly doubles the planned bound. The optimizer's smoothness/bound constraints only discipline the feedforward, not the feedback.

2. **This is another face of the "idealised" caveat.** A controller demanding ~5 g pivot acceleration with ~4000 m/s³ jerk during the catch is not something a real cart/actuator could track — the high-gain feedback that makes the near-uncontrollable catch work *requires* this violent, high-jerk motion. It's the same robustness razor's-edge (the 70k gains) showing up in the actuator-effort domain rather than the sensing domain.

If you want, I can (a) plot a(t) and jerk(t) so you can see the spike shape, or (b) add a **jerk/acceleration penalty** (penalize Δa between steps, and/or tighten the feedback during the catch) to the trajectory optimization and re-solve — though softening the catch feedback risks losing trackability, given how tight the margin is. Which would you like?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  06:13:30; model 11.5s

Plotted — pivot position, velocity, acceleration stacked vs time (the catch window 5–9 s shaded).

What the three panels show:
- **x (top):** the cart sweeps left to −4.5 m during the swing, then darts back to +1.6 m and parks — ~6 m of total travel for a unit-length chain.
- **dx/dt (middle):** velocity stays within the ±14 m/s bound (dotted), peaking ~−4 to +2.3 m/s during the catch, then →0.
- **d²x/dt² (bottom):** the smoking gun — gentle (≲5 m/s²) through the swing, then the catch spikes to **+50.7 m/s²**, double the nominal ±25 cap (dotted). That overshoot is the TVLQR feedback (gains ~70k) fighting the near-uncontrollable catch; the feedforward respected the cap, the feedback doesn't.

After ~9 s all three flatline — balanced and quiescent. The plot makes the core tension visual: a smooth, bounded *plan* but a violent, cap-busting *realized* control exactly where the chain passes through its uncontrollable configuration. That 5g/4000-jerk burst is the part a real actuator couldn't reproduce.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  06:29:43; model 40.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

The clean run is still churning (Stage 2's 9 direct N=6 solves on 9 workers — waiting on the slowest; controls not written yet). It'll finish and render via the chained task; I'll send the clean mp4 when it lands. Meanwhile, your two questions — which are the deep ones:

## Does this process still involve bend order?

**Yes — fundamentally.** The clean run *works* only because the seed (`swingup_N5_GOOD`) carries the right bend order. Note the subtlety: Stage 2's *selection criterion* is trackability, not bend order directly — it keeps whatever N=6 is trackable. But **whether a trackable N=6 even exists in a seed's family is determined by the bend order that seed carries.** From-scratch Stage 1 seeds (even ones scoring 4/4 closed-loop) often lack it, and then Stage 2 finds nothing. So the dependence is real; it's just "pre-satisfied" when we use the backed-up seed.

**Why bend order *is* controllability:** a trajectory whose chain goes dead-straight-and-still mid-swing passes through a near-uncontrollable configuration — a single horizontal pivot can't excite the internal bending modes of an aligned chain (the controllability matrix goes rank-deficient). That forces astronomical TVLQR gains (the 70k, and the 5g/4000-jerk you just saw). A trajectory that keeps a coordinated left-right *shimmy* — never dead-straight — stays controllable. The bend order literally *is* the trajectory's controllability profile.

## Is it possible to eliminate it?

Three levels, honestly:

1. **Reduce (pragmatic):** broaden Stage 2's target/horizon search so a trackable N=6 is found from a wider range of seeds. Covers more cases; doesn't remove the dependence.

2. **Eliminate (principled):** make controllability an **explicit objective** in the trajectory optimization — maximize the *minimum* controllability-Gramian singular value (or min σ of [B, AB, A²B, …]) along the path, or constrain it above a floor. Then the optimizer produces controllable, trackable trajectories **by construction, independent of seed bend order** — and as a bonus, lower required gains would tame the actuator violence. This is the real fix. Caveat: my earlier *naive* proxy (an anti-alignment penalty) failed — penalizing alignment isn't the same as maximizing the Gramian, and it just made trajectories more violent. A proper controllability-aware formulation is a genuine but tractable optimization task.

3. **Sidestep (architectural):** the root cause is one scalar input + high-gain TVLQR through a near-uncontrollable patch. A controllability-aware trajectory + lower-gain robust feedback, or feedback that detects low controllability and coasts, could reduce dependence — but single-input N=6 is intrinsically at the controllability edge.

**Bottom line:** bend order is still involved, and it *can* be eliminated in principle by **controllability-maximizing trajectory optimization** (level 2) — which would simultaneously kill the seed-dependence *and* the 5g actuator spikes, since both stem from the same near-uncontrollable transit. It's a real piece of optimization work (and my quick attempt didn't crack it), but it's the principled answer.

Want me to implement the controllability-aware objective (max min-Gramian-σ along the trajectory) and see if it produces a trackable N=6 directly — independent of bend order — and with gentler accelerations?

- **A (controllability-aware trajopt):** adds a min-controllability objective so a trackable N=6 emerges by construction from a neutral start — the principled "eliminate bend order" path. Bonus metric: does it also reduce the 5g/70k-gain spikes?

- **C (shortest pipeline):** strips all the pool/ranking/seed machinery down to a single mesh-refined N=2→6 homotopy ladder — tests whether the *natural* ladder N=6 just tracks, and checks reliability across repeats.

Each writes to its own `approachX_*` files (no collisions, the verified library and good seed untouched) and reports a common scorecard: does it work *without* the curated seed, wall-time, LOC/knobs, and gain/acceleration magnitudes.

## Verdict: the smaller-timestep robustness hypothesis is REFUTED.

Smaller dt does **not** widen the trackable set, does **not** rescue generic (wrong-bend-order) N=6 trajectories, and does **not** eliminate the seed/bend-order dependence. The dt=0.004 success is a narrow **sweet-spot window**, not a "smaller is better" threshold.

### Trackability-vs-dt table (full-state TVLQR, fine grid)

| trajectory | bend order | 0.010 | 0.008 | 0.006 | 0.005 | 0.0045 | 0.004 | 0.0035 | 0.003 | 0.002 | 0.001 | 0.0005 |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **curated** (T15, shipped seed) | `--+++` | . | **X** | **X** | **X** | **X** | **X** | . | . | . | . | . |
| generic (T13, from-scratch) | `+++++` | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . |
| generic (T16, from-scratch) | `+++++` | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . |
| generic (T16) | `+----` | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . |
| generic (T14, **fresh** ladder) | `-++-+` | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . | . |

(X = swings up to upright, final &lt; 0.05 rad; . = diverges mid-swing)

### The crux (does small dt rescue the wrong bend order?) — NO

- The **only** trackable trajectory is the curated bend-order `--+++` (the shipped good seed, confirmed identical: maxK=69448), and only in a **window** dt ∈ [~0.008, 0.004]. Below dt≈0.0035 it diverges **again**, at the same mid-swing instant (t≈7.97 s).
- Every **generic** bend order (`+++++`, `+----`, and the independently-generated fresh `-++-+`) diverges at **every** dt from 0.010 down to 0.0005 — always at a fixed mid-swing instant, independent of dt.
- As dt shrinks, the TVLQR gain `maxK` **grows monotonically** (curated 69k→82k; generics 100k–260k). The high-gain controller over-injects harder through the near-uncontrollable near-straight chain, so finer dt makes it *worse*, not better. dt=0.004 is a coincidental match between the ZOH step and this one trajectory's dynamics, not a controllability fix.
- Conclusion: the wrong-bend-order divergence is **genuinely (near-)uncontrollable**, not a discretization artifact. Small dt does not rescue it.

### dt threshold and its cost

- For the **curated** trajectory the trackable window is dt ∈ [~0.008, 0.004]; the shipped dt=0.004 sits safely inside it (going *finer* breaks it).
- **Sim-time cost** (TVLQR build + rollout; steps ∝ 1/dt): build dominates and scales ~linearly with 1/dt — about 2.0 s (dt=0.004) → 3.7 s (0.002) → 7.5 s (0.001) → 15 s (0.0005) for build, plus ~0.4→2.3 s rollout, per trajectory.
- **Optimization (IPOPT) cost is dt-independent** — same nominal regardless of sim dt (the fresh from-scratch N=2..5 ladder + one N=6 solve took ~25 min total here; that is the expensive part, and it is unchanged by dt). So "robustness via small dt" would have cost only sim time — but it doesn't buy robustness anyway.

### How much "magic" remains

All of it. The reproduction still depends entirely on the curated `--+++` bend-order seed. No tested dt (0.0005–0.010) makes any generic N=6 trajectory trackable. Smaller dt is not a path to a seed-independent N=6 swing-up.

### No bundle saved
Per task step 5, a `repro/approachB_controls.npz` was to be saved only **if** small dt makes a *generic* trajectory trackable. None did, so writing such a bundle would be misleading and I did not create one. (The single working combo — curated `--+++` at dt=0.004 — is already exactly what `repro/n6_controls.npz` ships.)

- `repro/approachB_dtscan.py` — generic-trajectory collection (reuse pool + fresh N=2..5→N=6 ladder) + dt-parameterized TVLQR/rollout/trackability check.
- `repro/approachB_landscape.py` — fine dt-grid trackability + maxK/divergence map.

<summary>Agent "Approach C: shortest ladder pipeline" completed</summary>
<result>Everything is verified. Here is my final report.

## Verdict: the minimal ladder pipeline does NOT produce a trackable N=6. The curated seed is necessary.

**Does the minimal mesh-refined homotopy ladder (N=2→3→4→5→6, target=zeros, coarse→fine, no pool/ranking/seed) yield a trackable N=6 out-of-the-box?** No — and not even close. It cannot produce a *converged* N=6 trajectory at all, let alone a trackable one.

### What I built
- `repro/approachC_build.py` (74 LOC) — the shortest self-contained ladder (N=2..5 coarse→fine, N=6 direct-fine), then `n6_perfect_state` trackability test at dt=0.004.
- `repro/approachC_sweep.py`, `repro/approachC_seedcheck.py` — diagnostic harnesses for the robustifying tweaks and the multi-seed robustness check.
- Logs: `runs/approachC_*.log`.

### Findings (in order of escalating machinery tried)
1. **N=5 rung is horizon-sensitive (knob #1 forced).** Plain ladder with target=zeros at **T=12** (the good-seed horizon) fails fine refinement ("Restoration Failed", constraint violation blows to 2.5e5). A horizon sweep found **T=11 converges** cleanly. So even getting an N=5 requires picking the horizon.
2. **The ladder N=5 lands in the right *coarse* class but wrong *fine* bend order.** Both the curated good seed and the ladder N=5 have net rev = **−0.5 per link** (identical homotopy class), but the ladder is whippier (max|θ̇| **27.4** vs the good seed's **23.2**).
3. **N=6 lift fails for every tweak (a) and (b).** Direct-fine N=6 from the ladder N=5 failed to converge for **all 6** combinations of horizon T∈{14,15,16} × terminal target∈{zeros, first+2π} — every IPOPT solve hit the iteration cap in restoration (`runs/approachC_sweep_s0b.log`). No `nosolve` even reached the trackability stage, so tweak (c) (smaller dt) is moot — there is no trajectory to track.
4. **Robustness across ladder seeds is poor (`runs/approachC_seedcheck.log`):** seed 0 builds N=5 but N=6 = NOSOLVE; **seeds 1 and 2 fail to build N=5 at all.** The plain ladder is not even reliable at the N=5 level.

### Contrast (anchoring the comparison)
The curated good seed (`repro/seeds/swingup_N5_GOOD.npz`) lifts to a trackable N=6 reliably — the existing `repro/n6_controls.npz` settles to **0.069°** (maxK 69448, dt=0.004). Same coarse homotopy class as the ladder, but its fine bend order is controllable. This confirms the README's subtle point precisely: **net revolutions are necessary but not sufficient — the fine-grained bend order must match a controllable topology, and a pure ladder doesn't reproduce it.**

### Measurements vs the current 2-stage repro
| | Approach C (ladder) | 2-stage (stage1+stage2) |
|---|---|---|
| LOC | 74 (build script) | 273 (155+118) + curated seed dep |
| Knobs needed | N=5 horizon + N=6 horizon + target — and still **fails** | N=5 bend-order via pool/ranking, or the backed-up seed |
| Wall-time | ~17 min just to *fail* the N=6 sweep | ~1–2 min from the good seed → **success** |
| Reliability | 0/3 ladder seeds yield a trackable (or even converged) N=6 | reliable from the good seed |
| Output | none (honestly unachievable) | `n6_controls.npz`, final 0.069° |

**Shorter?** Yes on LOC. **Faster / more robust / less magic?** No — it's slower (fails after grinding), non-robust (0/3 seeds), and the "magic" it removes (the curated seed / bend-order search) turns out to be **load-bearing**, not redundant.

- The hypothesis is **falsified**: the pool/ranking/seed machinery in the current repro is *not* unnecessary. The minimal sufficient pipeline still needs a source of the correct N=5 fine bend order, which the plain ladder cannot supply.</result>

## Report: Controllability-Aware Trajectory Optimization for N=6 Swing-Up

**Result: SUCCESS — a trackable N=6 swing-up was produced WITHOUT the curated seed.**

### The approach
I added an explicit controllability term to the N=6 collocation (`repro/approachA_optimize.py`, 383 LOC). The proxy, computed at subsampled nodes in CasADi:

- The pivot input enters as `M(θ)·θ̈ = -b·cosθ·a + …`, so the input-to-angular-acceleration direction is `u = M⁻¹(b⊙cosθ)`. I split `u` into the **rigid** rotation mode (all links together, direction `1`) and its **bending** complement in the kinetic-energy (M) metric, and take `c(θ) = ‖u_bend‖²_M`. This is the "B-direction excitation of the bending modes" — it collapses precisely when the chain goes near-straight (the documented N=6 failure) and is O(1) otherwise.
- **CasADi tractability fix:** `ca.solve` for `M⁻¹` breaks `expand=True` (LinsolQr has no `eval_sx`). I instead introduced `u` as extra decision vars with implicit constraint `M·u = b⊙cosθ`, and wrote `c = uᵀMu − (1ᵀMu)²/(1ᵀM1)` — fully SX-expandable.
- Used as a **one-sided soft floor** `w·Σ max(0, floor − √c)²` (penalize only collapse; a global reward fought the swing-up and never converged — 919s/fail). Optional hard floor also supported.
- Started from a **NEUTRAL** fresh cold homotopy ladder N=2→5 (target zeros, refined to h=0.01), lifted to N=6 — **no curated seed**. The neutral seed dips to cmin≈0.44 (goes near-straight; that's why it's normally untrackable).

### Metrics (winning case `soft_w100_fl0.8`, vs baseline)
| metric | Approach A | baseline (curated seed) |
|---|---|---|
| trackable (full-state, dt=0.004) | **yes, final 0.018°** | yes, 0.069° |
| maxK | **68110** | 69448 |
| max\|pivot accel\| (closed-loop) | **7.3 m/s²** | ~50 m/s² |

maxK is essentially unchanged (the high gain is intrinsic to N=6 near-straight mid-swing), but **closed-loop peak pivot acceleration dropped ~7× (50→7.3 m/s²)** — the controllability nudge removes the "5g spikes."

**Wall-clock:** neutral ladder ~255s (one-time, cached) + 8-candidate sweep ~240s on 8 workers ≈ **~8 min total** (≈4 min with the seed cached). Artifact saved to **`repro/approachA_controls.npz`** (exact `n6_perfect_state` bundle format; independently re-verified: 0.0184° upright, max accel 7.26 m/s²).

### Honest assessment of remaining "magic"
- **Seed dependence: ELIMINATED.** The trackable N=6 comes from a fresh neutral cold-start ladder to zeros; the curated `swingup_N5_GOOD.npz` is never read.
- **Magic shifted, not gone.** A robustness sweep (`runs/approachA_robust.log`) shows **4/15** (weight, floor) settings yield a trackable N=6, scattered (fl=0.6/w100, 0.8/w100, 0.85/w50, 0.85/w200) rather than a clean contiguous band. So you must sweep ~8-15 hyperparameter settings to reliably catch a winner — cheaper and more principled than hand-curating a seed, but not a single deterministic knob.
- **Key scientific finding:** the instantaneous controllability floor is *necessary but not sufficient*, confirming the PROGRESS.md bend-order caveat. **Moderate soft floors work; aggressive soft/hard floors (cmin forced ≥0.9-0.94) do NOT track** — they distort the trajectory into a different but still-untrackable bend order, with divergence just relocating to t≈9.6-10s. The gentle nudge works by bumping the natural swing-up out of its worst near-straight dip into a trackable bend-order basin, not by maximizing instantaneous controllability.

Files: `repro/approachA_optimize.py`, `repro/approachA_controls.npz`, `repro/approachA_pool/`, logs in `runs/approachA_*.log`.</result>

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  08:47:46; tool 90ms

```
def main():
    nworkers = int(sys.argv[1]) if len(sys.argv) > 1 else 8
    POOL.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    seed_path = POOL / "_neutral_seed_N5.npz"
    # clear stale candidate files (keep the cached neutral seed if present)
    for p in POOL.glob("*.npz"):
        if p.name != seed_path.name:
            p.unlink()

    if seed_path.exists() and "--rebuild" not in sys.argv:
        log("using cached NEUTRAL N=5 seed (NO curated seed; pass --rebuild to redo)")
        seed5 = dict(np.load(seed_path))
    else:
        log("building NEUTRAL homotopy ladder N=2..5 (target zeros, NO curated seed)...")
        seed5 = neutral_ladder()
        np.savez(seed_path, t=seed5["t"], theta=seed5["theta"], thetad=seed5["thetad"],
                 a=seed5["a"], v=seed5["v"], T=seed5["T"])
    chain5 = Chain(5, G)
    cseed = np.array([bend_excite_np(chain5, seed5["theta"][i])
                      for i in range(len(seed5["t"]))])
    log(f"  neutral N=5 seed ready (T={float(seed5['T'])}, cmin={cseed.min():.3f}, "
        f"cmed={np.median(cseed):.3f})")

    # Sweep the one-sided soft floor (w_ctrb, floor_ctrb) and the hard floor.
    # task = (tag, T, w_ctrb, floor_ctrb, hard_floor, seed_path)
    # w0 is the controllability-BLIND baseline from the SAME neutral start
    # (control). The soft cases penalize only bend-excitation below `floor`; the
    # hard cases constrain it >= floor. floor levels span the trackable band
    # (GOOD baseline never drops below ~0.97; neutral seed dips to ~0.44-0.60).
    sp = str(seed_path)
    tasks = [("w0_blind", 15.0, 0.0, 0.0, 0.0, sp)]                 # control
    for fl in (0.8, 0.9, 1.0):
        tasks.append((f"soft_w100_fl{fl}", 15.0, 100.0, fl, 0.0, sp))
    for hf in (0.85, 0.9, 0.95, 1.0):
        tasks.append((f"hard_fl{hf}", 15.0, 0.0, 0.0, hf, sp))

    log(f"solving {len(tasks)} controllability-aware N=6 ({nworkers} workers)...")
    with mp.Pool(nworkers) as pool:
        solved = [r for r in pool.map(w_solve, tasks) if r[1]]
    log(f"  {len(solved)}/{len(tasks)} solved")
    if not solved:
        raise SystemExit("no controllability-aware N=6 solved")

    log("evaluating trackability (full-state dt=0.004) + metrics...")
    with mp.Pool(nworkers) as pool:
        evals = pool.map(w_eval, [(t, f) for t, f, _ in solved])
    evals.sort(key=lambda e: (not e["ok"], e["final"]))
    log("results (sorted; ok first, then smallest upright error):")
    for e in evals:
        mk = e.get("maxK", float("nan")); am = e.get("accel_max", float("nan"))
        log(f"  {e['tag']:14s} ok={e['ok']!s:5s} final={np.degrees(e['final']):7.3f}deg "
            f"cmin={e['cmin']:.3f} maxK={mk:10.0f} accel_max={am:6.1f}")

    track = [e for e in evals if e["ok"]]
    if not track:
        best = evals[0]
        log(f"NO trackable N=6. closest: {best['tag']} final={np.degrees(best['final']):.3f}deg "
            f"cmin={best['cmin']:.3f}")
        raise SystemExit("no trackable N=6 (controllability-aware)")

    best = track[0]
    log(f"BEST trackable: {best['tag']} final={np.degrees(best['final']):.4f}deg "
        f"maxK={best.get('maxK'):.0f} accel_max={best.get('accel_max'):.1f}")
    _, _, bundle = n6_perfect_state(dict(np.load(best["fn"])))
    np.savez(OUT, **bundle)
    log(f"SAVED controls bundle -> {OUT} (maxK={bundle['maxK']:.0f}, "
        f"final={np.degrees(bundle['final']):.4f}deg)")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  08:56:13; tool 13ms

```
25	OUT = sys.argv[1] if len(sys.argv) > 1 else "repro/n6_swingup.mp4"
26	
27	
28	def simulate(c):
29	    """Full-state closed loop: a = a_ff + K (z_nom - z). Returns t, theta, x."""
30	    n, dt, g = int(c["n"]), float(c["dt"]), float(c["g"])
31	    chain = Chain(n, g)
32	    theta, thetad = c["theta_nom"], c["thetad_nom"]
33	    a_ff, v_nom, Ks = c["a_ff"], c["v_nom"], c["K"]
34	
35	    y = np.concatenate([theta[0], thetad[0]]); v = 0.0; x = 0.0
36	    T, X, TS = [y[:n].copy()], [x], [0.0]
37	    for k in range(len(Ks)):
38	        z = np.concatenate([y[:n], y[n:], [v]])
39	        zn = np.concatenate([theta[k], thetad[k], [v_nom[k]]])
40	        # TVLQR law: u = a_ff - K (z - z_nom)  (same convention as optimize_n6.py)
41	        a = a_ff[k] - float((Ks[k] @ (z - zn))[0])
42	        ynew = rk4_step(chain, y, a, dt)
43	        vnew = v + a * dt; x += 0.5 * (v + vnew) * dt
44	        y, v = ynew, vnew
45	        T.append(y[:n].copy()); X.append(x); TS.append((k + 1) * dt)
46	        if not np.isfinite(y).all():
47	            raise SystemExit(f"simulation diverged at t={k*dt:.2f}s")
48	    return np.array(TS), np.array(T), np.array(X)
49	
50	
51	def verify(theta, dt):
52	    n = theta.shape[1]
53	    wrap = lambda a: (a + np.pi) % (2 * np.pi) - np.pi
54	    tail = int(round(5.0 / dt))
55	    upright = np.all(np.abs(wrap(theta[-tail:])) < 0.10)  # within ~6 deg for last 5 s
56	    final = float(np.max(np.abs(wrap(theta[-1]))))
57	    return bool(upright), final
58	
59	
60	def animate(t, theta, x, out, fps=30):
61	    n = theta.shape[1]
62	    chain = Chain(n)
63	    # subsample frames to ~fps real-time
64	    step = max(1, int(round((1.0 / fps) / (t[1] - t[0]))))
65	    idx = np.arange(0, len(t), step)
66	    fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(5, 5))
67	    (line,) = ax.plot([], [], "o-", lw=2.5, ms=4)
68	    txt = ax.text(0.02, 0.97, "", transform=ax.transAxes, va="top", fontsize=9)
69	    ax.axhline(0, color="gray", lw=0.5); ax.set_aspect("equal")
70	    lim = n + 0.5; ax.set_ylim(-lim, lim)
71	
72	    def upd(j):
73	        i = idx[j]
74	        pts = chain.joint_positions(theta[i], x[i])
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  08:58:31; model 12.1s

Done — three approaches tried, winner found, the reproduction is now substantially more robust, less magic, and committed.

## Result of the 3-approach study

| Approach | Removes the magic? | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| Smaller dt | ❌ | Refuted — dt=0.004 is a *window*, not "smaller is better"; wrong bend order is genuinely uncontrollable at every dt |
| Minimal ladder | ❌ | Falsified — reproduces the coarse class but not the fine bend order; N=6 won't even converge (0/3) |
| **Controllability-aware trajopt** | ✅ | **Wins** — seed-free trackable N=6, *and* 7× gentler accelerations |

## The winner — `generate_n6.py` (seed-free)

It adds a soft floor on the **bend-mode excitation** `‖M⁻¹(b·cosθ)‖²_bend` — which collapses exactly when the chain goes near-straight — to the N=6 collocation, starting from a *neutral cold ladder* (no curated seed). This **produces** the controllable bend order instead of hand-curating it:
- **Seed dependence eliminated** — no `swingup_N5_GOOD.npz` needed.
- **final 0.018°** (better than the 0.069° seed path).
- **peak pivot accel 7.3 m/s²** vs ~50 — the 5g catch spikes you flagged are gone.

## Against your three axes
- **Least magic:** `generate_n6.py` — seed-free; the only remaining knob is a small parallel soft-floor sweep (principled, not curation).
- **Fastest:** `stage2_n6.py` from the backed-up seed (~1–2 min) — kept as the fast alternative.
- **Most robust / short:** the repro is now 5 clean scripts; `simulate_n6.py` hands off to the **balance LQR catch** after swing-up, so verification is robust to how late a gentle trajectory arrives (this is what flipped the earlier `FAIL` → `PASS`).

So the honest synthesis: the bend-order property is real and can't be *tolerated* away (dt) or *stumbled into* (naive ladder) — but it **can be produced by construction** with a controllability objective, which both removes the curated-seed magic and tames the actuator violence. The full comparison and usage are in `repro/README.md`; everything's committed.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  13:26:20; tool 86ms

```
#!/usr/bin/env python
"""Approach A: CONTROLLABILITY-AWARE trajectory optimization for N=6 swing-up.

GOAL: produce a TRACKABLE N=6 swing-up nominal WITHOUT the curated good N=5 seed
("no magic"). We start from a NEUTRAL homotopy ladder (target = zeros, fresh
cold ladder N=2..5 -> N=6) and add an explicit CONTROLLABILITY term to the
collocation so the optimizer keeps the chain in a controllable (trackable)
configuration by construction.

WHY THE BASELINE NEEDS MAGIC (from PROGRESS.md):
  Mid-swing, all 6 links pass through a near-STRAIGHT configuration. A straight
  chain is ~a single rigid body, so the internal BENDING modes become
  near-unactuatable from the one pivot input -> TVLQR gains explode (~7e4) and
  the closed loop diverges. Only trajectories whose "bend order" keeps the chain
  curved/shimmying (never dead-straight at the wrong moment) are trackable. The
  baseline gets that property only from a curated N=5 seed.

CONTROLLABILITY PROXY (principled, CasADi-cheap, well-scaled):
  The pivot input a enters the angular dynamics as  M(theta) tdd = -b*cos(theta)*a + ...
  so the INPUT-TO-ANGULAR-ACCELERATION direction is  u(theta) = M(theta)^{-1} (b o cos theta).
  Decompose u into the RIGID rotation mode (all links rotate together, direction
  1 = ones) and the BENDING complement, in the kinetic-energy (M) metric:
      u_rigid = (1^T M u)/(1^T M 1) * 1,   u_bend = u - u_rigid
  The controllability proxy at a node is the M-norm of the bending part:
      c(theta) = sqrt(u_bend^T M u_bend)
  This is exactly the "B-direction excitation of the bending modes" suggested by
  the task: how strongly the single input can directly drive the chain's
  internal shape. It collapses (-> small) precisely when the chain is straight
  (then u is almost pure rigid mode), and is O(1) and smooth otherwise. On the
  KNOWN-GOOD baseline nominal it never drops below ~0.97; on naive cold-start
  N=6 nominals it dips near 0 at the straight crossing. We REWARD it (soft) and/
  or FLOOR it (hard), driving the optimizer to a trackable bend order from a
  neutral start.

We sweep the soft weight w and the hard floor, solve each on neutral warm
starts, then test every result with repro.optimize_n6.n6_perfect_state at
dt=0.004 (full-state TVLQR). SUCCESS = ok=True. We report maxK and max|pivot
accel| (controllability-awareness should reduce both vs baseline maxK~69448).

Run:  uv run python repro/approachA_optimize.py [n_workers]
"""
import sys, os, pathlib, time
sys.path.insert(0, str(pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]))

import numpy as np
import warnings; warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
import casadi as ca
import multiprocessing as mp

from pendulum.dynamics import Chain
from pendulum.trajopt import (chain_constants, make_M_rhs_fn,
                              solve_swingup_implicit, homotopy_guess)
from repro.optimize_n6 import n6_perfect_state

G = 9.81
N = 6
A_MAX, V_MAX = 25.0, 14.0
SETTLE_FRAC, SETTLE_BAND = 0.08, 0.15
POOL = pathlib.Path("repro/pool_ctrb")
OUT = "repro/n6_controls.npz"

_t0 = time.monotonic()
def log(m): print(f"[{time.monotonic()-_t0:7.1f}s] {m}", flush=True)


# ---- controllability proxy (CasADi) ---------------------------------------
def bend_excite_ca(theta, u, A):
    """Squared M-norm of the bending (non-rigid) part of the input-to-angular-
    acceleration direction u, where u solves  M(theta) u = b o cos(theta)
    (enforced as a separate IMPLICIT constraint, so NO symbolic matrix inverse
    appears here -> the whole NLP stays SX-expandable, unlike ca.solve which
    uses LinsolQr and breaks expand=True).

    With Mu = M u (computable, no inverse) the bending M-norm is
        ||u_bend||_M^2 = u^T M u - (1^T M u)^2 / (1^T M 1)
    because the rigid mode is 1=ones and the projection is M-orthogonal.
    theta,u: (n,1) MX. Returns scalar MX (well-scaled, O(1), smooth)."""
    n = A.shape[0]
    Aca = ca.DM(A); ones = ca.DM(np.ones((n, 1)))
    dth = ca.repmat(theta, 1, n) - ca.repmat(theta.T, n, 1)
  
… [truncated 1391 chars]
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  13:26:30; tool 108ms

```
    """Trapezoidal IMPLICIT collocation (same skeleton as trajopt's) PLUS a
    controllability term that targets ONLY the configurations where the chain
    goes near-straight (the documented failure):

      ONE-SIDED soft penalty  w_ctrb * sum_k max(0, floor_ctrb - sqrt(c_k))^2
      (active only where bend-excitation sqrt(c) drops below floor_ctrb; healthy
       nodes are untouched, so it does NOT fight the swing-up globally), and/or
      a HARD floor  sqrt(c_k) >= hard_floor.

    c = ||u_bend||_M^2 (squared bend excitation), with u defined implicitly by
    M u = b o cos(theta) (extra decision vars, no symbolic inverse).
    """
    n = N
    A, b = chain_constants(n)
    if theta_target is None:
        theta_target = np.zeros(n)
    theta_target = np.asarray(theta_target, float)
    h = T / K
    Mfn, rfn = make_M_rhs_fn(n, G)

    opti = ca.Opti()
    TH = opti.variable(n, K + 1); TD = opti.variable(n, K + 1)
    VV = opti.variable(1, K + 1); TDD = opti.variable(n, K + 1)
    AC = opti.variable(1, K + 1)

    cost = 0
    for k in range(K + 1):
        opti.subject_to(ca.mtimes(Mfn(TH[:, k]), TDD[:, k])
                        == rfn(TH[:, k], TD[:, k], AC[0, k]))
    for k in range(K):
        opti.subject_to(TH[:, k + 1] - TH[:, k] == 0.5 * h * (TD[:, k] + TD[:, k + 1]))
        opti.subject_to(TD[:, k + 1] - TD[:, k] == 0.5 * h * (TDD[:, k] + TDD[:, k + 1]))
        opti.subject_to(VV[0, k + 1] - VV[0, k] == 0.5 * h * (AC[0, k] + AC[0, k + 1]))
        cost += 0.5 * h * (AC[0, k] ** 2 + AC[0, k + 1] ** 2)        # min effort
        cost += 1e-3 * (AC[0, k + 1] - AC[0, k]) ** 2                 # smoothness

    # boundary
    opti.subject_to(TH[:, 0] == np.pi); opti.subject_to(TD[:, 0] == 0)
    opti.subject_to(VV[0, 0] == 0)
    opti.subject_to(TH[:, K] == theta_target); opti.subject_to(TD[:, K] == 0)
    opti.subject_to(VV[0, K] == 0)
    opti.subject_to(opti.bounded(-A_MAX, ca.vec(AC), A_MAX))
    opti.subject_to(opti.bounded(-V_MAX, VV, V_MAX))

    kset = int(round((1 - SETTLE_FRAC) * K))
    for k in range(kset, K + 1):
        opti.subject_to(opti.bounded(theta_target - SETTLE_BAND, TH[:, k],
                                     theta_target + SETTLE_BAND))

    # CONTROLLABILITY term over the swing (skip the locked-down start/settle ends)
    # Subsample nodes (CSTRIDE) to keep the extra implicit u-vars cheap; the
    # bend-excitation varies smoothly so a stride of a few nodes is plenty.
    CSTRIDE = 3
    k_lo = max(1, int(0.05 * K)); k_hi = kset
    cnodes = list(range(k_lo, k_hi, CSTRIDE))
    use_ctrb = (w_ctrb > 0.0 and floor_ctrb > 0.0) or hard_floor > 0.0
    if use_ctrb and cnodes:
        U = opti.variable(n, len(cnodes))   # input->angaccel direction at cnodes
        for j, k in enumerate(cnodes):
            # implicit definition: M(theta_k) u_k = b o cos(theta_k)  (no inverse)
            opti.subject_to(ca.mtimes(mass_matrix_ca(TH[:, k], A), U[:, j])
                            == bend_rhs_ca(TH[:, k], A, b))
            c = bend_excite_ca(TH[:, k], U[:, j], A)    # squared bend excitation
            cm = ca.sqrt(c + 1e-9)                       # bend-excitation magnitude
            if w_ctrb > 0.0 and floor_ctrb > 0.0:
                short = ca.fmax(0.0, floor_ctrb - cm)    # one-sided hinge
                cost += w_ctrb * short * short           # penalize only collapse
            if hard_floor > 0.0:
                opti.subject_to(cm >= hard_floor)        # hard floor

    opti.minimize(cost)

    # neutral warm start (homotopy guess or pi->target ramp)
    s = np.linspace(0, 1, K + 1)
    if init_guess is not None:
        Kg = init_guess["theta"].shape[0] - 1; sg = np.linspace(0, 1, Kg + 1)
        thg = np.array([np.interp(s, sg, init_guess["theta"][:, j]) for j in range(n)])
        tdg = np.array([np.interp(s, sg, init_guess["thetad"][:, j]) for j in range(n)])
        vg = np.interp(s, sg, init_guess["v"]); ag = np.interp(s, sg, init_guess["a"])
        opti.set_initial(TH, 
… [truncated 5352 chars]
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:28:47; model 12.7s

N=7 search launched and climbing. The setup, for context:

**Generalized the controllability-aware approach to arbitrary N** (`repro/generate_nN.py`) — same soft-floor-on-bend-excitation idea, with two N=7-specific extensions:
1. **Ladder extended to N=6** (the neutral seed for the N=7 lift) — already converged cleanly (N=5→6 in ~16 s).
2. **dt sweep added** {0.004 … 0.0015} — because N=7's instability is faster (λ≈20.6 vs 18.3/s), its trackable dt-window is likely *narrower and at smaller dt* than N=6's [0.008, 0.004], per Approach B's finding. So each candidate trajectory is tested across dt to find its window.

The honest expectation: N=7 is materially harder than N=6 — the catch basin is ~1.4×10⁻⁴ rad (5× tighter), TVLQR gains will be even higher, and whether the controllability floor can produce a trackable bend order at *that* tightness is genuinely uncertain. The two things that could block it:
- the controllability-aware N=7 solve (15-state) failing to converge (it fought convergence even at N=6), or
- no (floor, dt) combination clearing the much tighter terminal-accuracy bar.

The monitor will report `seed ready → solved → floor=… → SAVED` or where it stalls. If it finds a trackable N=7, I'll verify (swing-up + catch) and render the mp4. If it stalls at a specific stage, that stall location is itself the informative result about where N=7 hits the wall. Reporting at the next milestone.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  14:08:26; model 37.1s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

**Decisive — and deeper than a gain wall.** Even with gentle gains (high R drops maxK to ~4000, *below* N=6's 68k), N=7 is **untrackable at every (r, dt) combination**. So it's not gain *magnitude* — there's simply **no gain that stabilizes the N=7 trajectory**. That points to the real cause:

The scalar controllability floor that worked for N=6 is **insufficient for N=7's richer mode structure**. A 7-link chain has *6 bending modes*; my proxy lumps them into one aggregate "bend excitation" and floors the total. Keeping the *aggregate* above 0.8 (cmin=0.81) doesn't guarantee *each individual mode* is excitable from the single pivot — so one bending mode can be effectively uncontrollable mid-swing even though the aggregate looks healthy, and then no TVLQR gain (low or high) can hold it.

This is a clean frontier result:
- **N≤5:** full swing-up + balance, realistic observer.
- **N=6:** full-state swing-up, seed-free via *scalar* controllability shaping (the magic removed).
- **N=7:** beyond this architecture — even full-state + gentle gains + scalar controllability shaping can't track it; the single-mode proxy doesn't ensure all 6 bending modes stay controllable.

Let me confirm the 4th candidate doesn't break the pattern, then I'll write it up:

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  14:09:35; model 13.4s

Clean and committed. Here's the honest result of extending to N=7.

## N=7 is a genuine frontier wall — and we found *why*

I generalized the controllability-aware approach (`repro/generate_nN.py`, works for any N — reproduces N=6) and seeded N=7 from our clean N=6 trajectory (gentle, θ̇≈20). The 4 controllability-aware N=7 candidates converged, but:

- **None trackable at any dt** in [0.004, 0.015] — even the well-controlled, gentle ones (cmin≈0.81, θ̇≈19).
- **Not a gain-magnitude wall:** a TVLQR weight sweep dropped maxK to ~4000 (*below* N=6's 68k) and it *still* diverges at every (R, dt). So **no gain stabilizes the N=7 trajectory** — it's not "gains too high," it's "trajectory not stabilizable."

**The cause** (the valuable part): the **scalar** controllability proxy that removed the magic at N=6 is **insufficient at N=7**. A 7-link chain has *6 bending modes*; my floor keeps the *aggregate* bend-excitation healthy, but that doesn't guarantee *each individual mode* stays excitable from the single pivot. One mode can go effectively uncontrollable mid-swing while cmin looks fine — and then nothing can hold it.

## The frontier, cleanly delineated

| N | Result |
|---|---|
| 1–5 | Full swing-up + balance, **realistic observer** |
| 6 | Full-state swing-up, **seed-free** via scalar controllability shaping (magic removed) |
| 7 | **Beyond this architecture** — even full-state + gentle gains + scalar shaping can't track it |

This matches the literature trajectory (published swing-up tops out at triple; each added link is dramatically harder).

## The principled next step (if you want to push further)

Replace the *scalar* aggregate floor with a **per-mode controllability constraint** — maximize/floor the *minimum singular value* of the input-to-bending-mode coupling across *all* 6 modes, not just the aggregate. That would ensure every bending mode stays excitable along the path. It's a significantly harder NLP (eigenvalue/SVD constraints in CasADi, convergence will fight back — the scalar version already did), with no guarantee, but it's the right direction and directly addresses the diagnosed cause.

Want me to attempt the per-mode controllability formulation for N=7, or is the characterized wall the right place to stop?
